         <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">
          Recife
         </a>
         , Brazil. The country is a featured tourism destination.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In recent decades the economies of South America have been transformed into fully competitive and efficient markets. In recent years, one characteristic of the economy of UNASUR has been its excessive growth and high competitiveness, leading to world profits alongside China and India. This economic situation is marked by policies favoring market opening, aimed at the exploitation of natural resources, industrialization and a very attractive destination for investors. In spite of all this, the situation is marked by immense regional differences and by an irregularity in the distribution of the income that stands out at world level, although it is recognized as one of the regions of the world where poverty and inequality have been reduced more energetically in recent decades.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are regions with very high industrialization, where the main economic flows move, while there are sectors where there are hardly any industries. Most of the possessions are concentrated in the hands of a minority of the population, whereas millions of individuals experience different levels of privations arriving, in extreme cases, to the absolute poverty. However, it is necessary to emphasize that poverty in South America has been reduced in a surprising way, especially in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">
        Southern Cone
       </a>
       and North of South America. Today, thanks to the development of many South American nations, it has allowed the world, their eyes on some governments, even forming part of economic blocs like
       <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">
        G20
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">
        BRICS
       </a>
       . Although this reality is common to the entire South American group, the countries of the so-called Southern Cone (Argentina,
       <a href="/wiki/South_Region,_Brazil" title="South Region, Brazil">
        southern Brazil
       </a>
       , Chile, and Uruguay) present more positive socioeconomic data and high
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">
        HDI
       </a>
       rates.
      </p>
      <p>
       The South American economy is divided between the mineral extractivism in the Amazon region and the agriculture present in practically all its States. Industrialization is of medium level to high in diverse regions, although very strong the presence of local industries of origin Foreign (multinational). The extraction and export of oil is notable in Venezuela, which owns some of the largest world reserves, in Argentina and in the Atlantic Ocean compared to the Brazilian states of
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">
        Rio de Janeiro
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">
        São Paulo
       </a>
       . Bolivia stands out for the production of natural gas, with important reserves of this matter that in recent years have led to what has been known as the "Gas War."
      </p>
      <p>
       The richest and most industrialized regions of the continent are: São Paulo State in Brazil, where its main financial center (in its capital), the main technological centers in South America (
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Carlos" title="São Carlos">
        São Carlos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_dos_Campos" title="São José dos Campos">
        São José dos Campos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">
        Campinas
       </a>
       ) and its largest and most mobile port -; Followed by the Fluvial-Industrial axis of Paraná between
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosario" title="Rosario">
        Rosario
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/La_Plata" title="La Plata">
        La Plata
       </a>
       in Argentina centered in Buenos Aires (second most active port and city with higher GDP); And for the also Brazilian State of Rio de Janeiro.
      </p>
      <p>
       Brazil and Argentina are considered the regional leaders of South America. They are the two largest nations and the two largest economies in South America. These are the only South American countries that are members of the G-20 and Brazil, specially, as member of the BRICS. They're also the largest producers and exporters of agricultural products of the continent.
      </p>
      <p>
       The highest
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">
        nominal GDP
       </a>
       in 2017 is Brazil (8th worldwide) with 2,140,940 trillion dollars, followed by Argentina (21th worldwide) with 628,935 billion dollars, and Colombia (31st at the global level) with 306,439 billion dollars.
      </p>
      <p>
       The highest
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">
        GDP
       </a>
       in 2017 is in Brazil (8th worldwide) with 3,216,031 trillion dollars, Argentina (27th worldwide) with 912,816 billion dollars, and Colombia (31st Worldwide) with 720,151 billion dollars.
      </p>
      <p>
       The highest
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">
        GDP per capita
       </a>
       in 2017 is held by Chile with US$24,113, followed by Uruguay with 21,527 and Argentina with 20,047. In terms of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">
        nominal per capita GDP
       </a>
       , the ranking is headed by Uruguay with US$15,679, Chile with US$13,576, and Argentina with US$12,503.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Common_Market">
        Common Market
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Common Market">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Initiative_for_the_Integration_of_the_Regional_Infrastructure_of_South_America" title="Initiative for the Integration of the Regional Infrastructure of South America">
        Initiative for the Integration of the Regional Infrastructure of South America
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1052" data-file-width="744" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg/180px-Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg/270px-Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg/360px-Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_member_states_of_unasur_english.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Members of UNASUR and main regional highways.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of the initiatives of Unasur is the creation of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_market" title="Common market">
        common market
       </a>
       , starting with the elimination of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tariffs" title="Tariffs">
        tariffs
       </a>
       for products considered non-sensitive until 2014 and for sensitive products until 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Initiative_for_the_Integration_of_the_Regional_Infrastructure_of_South_America" title="Initiative for the Integration of the Regional Infrastructure of South America">
        Initiative for the Integration of the Regional Infrastructure of South America
       </a>
       is currently underway, with investments estimated at US$38 billion from the
       <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">
        Inter-American Development Bank
       </a>
       , the Andean Development Corporation, the
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Development_Bank" title="Brazilian Development Bank">
        National Bank for Economic and Social Development
       </a>
       and the Financial Fund for Development of the Plata Basin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Integração_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Integração-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The initial integration plans through the infrastructure cooperation of UNASUR came with the construction of the Bioceanic Corridor and the
       <a href="/wiki/Interoceanic_Highway" title="Interoceanic Highway">
        Interoceanic Highway
       </a>
       . Roads that will link more firmly the countries of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_coast" title="Pacific coast">
        Pacific coast
       </a>
       , especially Chile and Peru, with the countries of the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic coast
       </a>
       like Brazil and Argentina, extending highways through the continent, allowing better connections of the ports to Bolivia and more internal parts of Argentina, Peru And Brazil. The Pacific Highway, between Peru and Brazil, began to be built in September 2005, financed 60% by Brazil and 40% by Peru, and was completed in December 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Integração_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Integração-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The South American Energy Ring will interconnect Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Paraguay and Uruguay with natural gas from various sources, such as the Camisea Gas project in Peru and the Tarija gas deposits in Bolivia. Although this proposal has been signed and ratified, political and economic difficulties in Argentina and Bolivia have delayed this initiative, and to this day, this agreement remains more a protocol than a current project, since Chile and Brazil are already building LNG terminals for Gas from external suppliers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Integração_53-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Integração-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_development">
        Economic development
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economic development">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg/250px-GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg/375px-GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg/500px-GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GDP_PPP_2016_Selection_EN.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Selection of GDP PPP data (top 10 countries and blocks) in no particular order
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Presidents of the seven founding countries (Argentina, Bolivia, Brazil, Ecuador, Paraguay, Venezuela and Uruguay) officially launched the South American Bank in Buenos Aires in December 2007. The heads of all the founding countries were at the ceremony, with the exception of President
       <a href="/wiki/Tabar%C3%A9_V%C3%A1zquez" title="Tabaré Vázquez">
        Tabaré Vázquez
       </a>
       of Uruguay. The capital will be US$7b, with Venezuela responsible for US$3b and Brazil US$2b. The headquarters will be located in Caracas with offices in Buenos Aires and La Paz.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MercoPress1_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MercoPress1-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc1-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">
        Bank of the South
       </a>
       will finance economic development projects to improve local competitiveness and to promote the scientific and technological development of the member states. Its founding charter affirms that the bank will promote projects in a "stable and equal" manner and priorities will be oriented towards reinforcing South American integration, reducing asymmetries, and promoting an egalitarian distribution of investments.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Brazilian Minister, Guido Mantega, stated that the bank is not similar to the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        International Monetary Fund
       </a>
       ; it will be a credit institution similar to the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Monetary_policy">
        Monetary policy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Monetary policy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Single_South_American_currency" title="Single South American currency">
        Single South American currency
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">
        Bank of the South
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banco_del_Sur.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1442" data-file-width="2100" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Banco_del_Sur.jpg/250px-Banco_del_Sur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Banco_del_Sur.jpg/375px-Banco_del_Sur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Banco_del_Sur.jpg/500px-Banco_del_Sur.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banco_del_Sur.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">
          Rafael Correa
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">
          Evo Morales
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">
          Néstor Kirchner
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Cristina Fernández">
          Cristina Fernández
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">
          Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Nicanor_Duarte" title="Nicanor Duarte">
          Nicanor Duarte
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">
          Hugo Chávez
         </a>
         at the signing of the founding charter of the Bank of the South
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">
        Bank of the South
       </a>
       (Portuguese: Banco do Sul, Spanish: Banco del Sur, Dutch: Bank van het Zuiden, English: Bank of the South) will establish monetary policy and finance development projects. One of the objectives of monetary union is to establish a
       <a href="/wiki/Single_South_American_currency" title="Single South American currency">
        Single South American currency
       </a>
       . Support for the creation of this currency was provided in January 2007 by Peruvian President
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Alan García">
        Alan García
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and other South American authorities expressed themselves in favor, as Bolivian President
       <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">
        Evo Morales
       </a>
       in April of that year, who proposed that the currency Only one denominated "Pacha" ("earth" in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">
        Quechua language
       </a>
       ), however, except for the right of each country to suggest a name for the common currency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The South American economy is divided between mineral industry in the Amazon region and agriculture, which is present in practically all member states. Industrialization is advanced in several regions, although there is a strong presence of local industries of foreign (multinational) origin. In Brazil and Argentina the level of industrialization is intense.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Defense_policy">
        Defense policy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Defense policy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_American_Defense_Council" title="South American Defense Council">
        South American Defense Council
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Unasul_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1185" data-file-width="1835" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Unasul_1.jpg/220px-Unasul_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Unasul_1.jpg/330px-Unasul_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Unasul_1.jpg/440px-Unasul_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Unasul_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Soldier of the
         <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">
          Brazilian Army
         </a>
         patrols the surroundings of the Summit of Heads of State of Unasur in 2008, held in Brasilia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_American_Defense_Council" title="South American Defense Council">
        South American Defense Council
       </a>
       (CDS) was proposed by Venezuela and Brazil to serve as a mechanism for regional security, promoting military co-operation. From the beginning Brazil, Argentina and Chile, the countries that took the leadership of the project, made clear that they did not intend to form a
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       -like alliance, but a cooperative security arrangement, enhancing multilateral military cooperation, promoting confidence and security building measures and fostering defense industry exchange. Colombia initially refused to join the defense council due to the strong military ties it has with the United States through the
       <a href="/wiki/Plan_Colombia" title="Plan Colombia">
        Plan Colombia
       </a>
       . However, after reviewing the proposal they decided to join on 20 July 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecodiario1_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ecodiario1-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-people1_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-people1-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Shortly following the signing by Colombia's President, President of Chile
       <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">
        Michelle Bachelet
       </a>
       appointed a working group to investigate and draft a plan for the new council. Finally, on 10 March 2009, the 12 nation members held, in Chile, the first meeting of the newly formed council.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coha1_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-coha1-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In mid-2010, UNASUR played a key role in mediating the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_Colombia%E2%80%93Venezuela_diplomatic_crisis" title="2010 Colombia–Venezuela diplomatic crisis">
        2010 Colombia–Venezuela diplomatic crisis
       </a>
       . On 1 September 2010, the agency "UnasurHaití" was created to provide US$100 million in help to Haiti.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pagina12_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pagina12-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Democracy">
        Democracy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Democracy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2490" data-file-width="3312" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg/220px-Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg/330px-Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg/440px-Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bicentenario_Argentina_-_Presidentes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         South American presidents in front of the
         <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosada" title="Casa Rosada">
          Casa Rosada
         </a>
         , Buenos Aires, during the bicentenary of the
         <a href="/wiki/May_Revolution" title="May Revolution">
          May Revolution
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 26 November 2010, the Additional Protocol on Commitment to Democracy was signed in the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">
        Georgetown
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperative_Republic_of_Guyana" title="Cooperative Republic of Guyana">
        Cooperative Republic of Guyana
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The protocol derives from the mandate established in the Buenos Aires Declaration of 1 October 2010, which affirms that member states will not tolerate a challenge to institutional authority, nor attempt to strike a legitimately constituted civilian power, adopting concrete and immediate measures in case of breach of constitutional order. It is applicable "in the event of a breach or threat of a breach of the democratic order, of a violation of the constitutional order or in any situation that endangers the legitimate exercise of power and the observance of democratic values and principles."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Democracia_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Democracia-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the event of such a situation, the Council of Heads of State and Government or the Council of Ministers of Foreign Affairs may be convened extraordinarily by the Pro-Tempore Presidency of the Union, ex officio or at the request of the affected State or another member of UNASUR, to deliberate on the application of sanctions to the affected state. Among the political and diplomatic sanctions envisaged by the Protocol, the following stand out:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Democracia_64-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Democracia-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Suspension of the right to participate in the different organs and instances of Unasur
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Democracia_64-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Democracia-64">
          [64]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Partial or total closure of land borders with the affected State, including suspension or limitation of trade, air and sea transportation, communications, energy supply, services and supply.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Free_movement_of_people">
        Free movement of people
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Free movement of people">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_(cortado).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2412" data-file-width="1768" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_%28cortado%29.jpg/150px-Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_%28cortado%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_%28cortado%29.jpg/225px-Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_%28cortado%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_%28cortado%29.jpg/300px-Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_%28cortado%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Passaporte_brasileiro_2015_(cortado).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_passport" title="Brazilian passport">
          Brazilian passport
         </a>
         with the indication of
         <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">
          Mercosur
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Visits by South American citizens to any South American independent country of up to 90 days only require an identification document issued by the traveler's country. In November 2006, Argentina, Bolivia, Brazil, Chile, Colombia, Ecuador, Guyana, Paraguay, Peru, Suriname, and Uruguay agreed to abolish visa requirements for tourists between any of those nations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Mercosur, along with its Associate members of Bolivia, Chile, Colombia and Ecuador established that their territories together form an "area of free residence with the right to work" to all its citizens, with no additional requirements other than nationality. The Free Movement and Residence Agreement was established in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">
        Brasília
       </a>
       summit based in a previous document signed on 6 December 2002.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Citizens of any Mercosur countries will have a simplified process in temporary residence visa of up to two years in any other member countries, with the requirements of a valid passport,
       <a href="/wiki/Birth_certificate" title="Birth certificate">
        birth certificate
       </a>
       , and no criminal record. Temporary residence can become permanent if a licit means of living can be verified.
      </p>
      <p>
       At a summit in Guayaquil, Ecuador on 4 December 2014, UNASUR general secretary Ernesto Samper announced, "We have approved the concept of South American citizenship," including the creation of a single passport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_monitors">
        Electoral monitors
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Electoral monitors">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       UNASUR has also initiated the creation of
       <a href="/wiki/Election_monitoring" title="Election monitoring">
        electoral monitor teams
       </a>
       that could replace the monitors from the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_nation_states">
        Participating nation states
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Participating nation states">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Member states of the Union of South American Nations">
        Member states of the Union of South American Nations
       </a>
      </div>

         </a>

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following territories situated outside South America are part of member states and therefore participate:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">
         Easter Island
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         Rapa Nui
        </i>
        ), a Chilean territory situated in Oceania.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Archipelago_of_San_Andr%C3%A9s,_Providencia_and_Santa_Catalina" title="Archipelago of San Andrés, Providencia and Santa Catalina">
         San Andrés y Providencia
        </a>
        , a Colombian territory situated in Central America.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Isla_Aves" title="Isla Aves">
         Isla Aves
        </a>
        , a Venezuelan territory situated in the
        <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">
         Antilles
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_of_Antarctica" title="Territorial claims of Antarctica">
         Argentine and Chilean Antarctic
        </a>
        bases.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Non-participating_South_American_states_and_territories">
        Non-participating South American states and territories
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Non-participating South American states and territories">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following parts of South America are territories of non-South American states and therefore do not participate:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Aruba,
        <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
         Bonaire
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">
         Curaçao
        </a>
        are parts of the Kingdom of the Netherlands near the Venezuelan coastline.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">
         French Guiana
        </a>
        , which is an
        <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" title="Overseas department">
         overseas department
        </a>
        of France and is therefore part of the
        <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
         European Union
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">
         Falkland Islands
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">
         South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands
        </a>
        , which are
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">
         overseas territories
        </a>
        of the United Kingdom
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
         <a href="#cite_note-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union#Overseas_countries_and_territories" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">
         overseas countries and territories
        </a>
        of the European Union;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
         <a href="#cite_note-71">
          [71]
         </a>
        </sup>
        they are also claimed by Argentina.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
         <a href="#cite_note-72">
          [72]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Trinidad and Tobago, although not a member, was invited to join the Union of South American Nations by President of Venezuela,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicolas_Maduro" title="Nicolas Maduro">
         Nicolas Maduro
        </a>
        in July 2013.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
         <a href="#cite_note-73">
          [73]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereignty_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Sovereignty of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">
           Sovereignty of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands
          </a>
          .
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-73">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-73">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation news">
           Johnlall, Raphael (18 July 2013).
           <a class="external text" href="http://guardian.co.tt/business-guardian/2013-07-17/venezuela-president-maduro-talked-energy-transport-while-tt" rel="nofollow">
            "Venezuela President Maduro talked energy, transport while in T&amp;T"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Guardian" title="Trinidad and Tobago Guardian">
             Trinidad and Tobago Guardian
            </a>
           </i>
           . Guardian Media
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             29 September
            </span>
            2013
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            Apart from Mercosur, Maduro also invited T&amp;T to be "incorporated" into Union of South American Nations (Unasur) because of its geographical proximity to the South American mainland." Maduro said.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Trinidad+and+Tobago+Guardian&amp;rft.atitle=Venezuela+President+Maduro+talked+energy%2C+transport+while+in+T%26T&amp;rft.date=2013-07-18&amp;rft.aulast=Johnlall&amp;rft.aufirst=Raphael&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fguardian.co.tt%2Fbusiness-guardian%2F2013-07-17%2Fvenezuela-president-maduro-talked-energy-transport-while-tt&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnion+of+South+American+Nations">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-74">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-74">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="external free" href="http://cadmus.eui.eu/bitstream/handle/1814/20394/RSCAS_2012_05.pdf?sequence=1" rel="nofollow">
           http://cadmus.eui.eu/bitstream/handle/1814/20394/RSCAS_2012_05.pdf?sequence=1
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
